Situation: The village holds its annual baking contest. Three bakers compete: Tessa (PC), Old Marta (NPC), and Young Finn (NPC). The winner earns the Golden Whisk and bragging rights for a year.

Action: Each baker rolls Baking (DC 18, Bake to Impress). Tessa rolls 19 (success), Marta rolls 16 (partial), Finn rolls 11 (fail).

Outcome: Tessa’s berry tart wins first place. Marta’s bread is delicious but slightly underbaked. Finn’s cookies are edible but unremarkable. Tessa earns the Golden Whisk tag and Advantage on her next social check with the mayor.

Example 2: Mediating a Fence Dispute

Situation: Two farmers, Gregor and Hilda, argue over a shared fence. Gregor wants to replace it with stone; Hilda prefers wood. The PC mediator steps in.

Action: The GM calls for Mediation (DC 16, Broker Agreement). The mediator rolls 17 (success).

Outcome: The mediator suggests a compromise: a wood fence with stone posts. Both farmers agree. The GM notes that the mediator has earned the Trusted Mediator tag, granting Advantage on future social checks in the village.

Example 3: Tending the Herd During a Storm

Situation: A sudden storm spooks the sheep herd. The herder must calm the animals and check for injuries before they scatter.

Action: The GM calls for Animal Husbandry (DC 16, Calm Spooked Animals). The herder rolls 14 (partial).

Outcome: Most of the sheep calm down, but two lambs wander off. The GM starts a clock: “Find Lost Lambs” (4 segments). The herder must track them before nightfall.

Using Cozy Skills

Cozy skills reward patience, preparation, and care. They create spaces where characters connect, build, and solve problems without violence. When using these skills:

  • Celebrate Small Victories: A perfect loaf of bread or a resolved dispute is a meaningful success.
  • Use Clocks for Long-Term Goals: Track festival preparations, garden growth, or community projects with clocks (see Chapter 05).
  • Layer Social Stakes: Cozy games thrive on relationships. Failed checks can strain friendships, but successes build trust and community.
  • Encourage Downtime: Many cozy skills shine during downtime. Let players bake, garden, or host without time pressure.

For proficiencies that enhance these skills, see Chapter 13 (Cozy Proficiencies). For tags and conditions, see Chapter 18 (Tags and Conditions Glossary).

Chapter 08: Fantasy Genre Skills

Fantasy games celebrate heroism, magic, exploration, and the clash of steel. These skills turn dungeons into navigable challenges, courtly intrigue into narrative battlefields, and arcane mysteries into solvable puzzles. They are grounded in genre conventions where brave heroes face monsters, uncover ancient secrets, and shape the fate of kingdoms.

This chapter provides ready-to-use skills for fantasy games—whether high fantasy quests, gritty sword-and-sorcery, or magical realism. Use these skills when your game features adventurers, magic, wilderness survival, and combat.

Genre Overview

Fantasy skills emphasize:

  • Combat Prowess: Melee Combat, Archery, Tactics—skills for surviving and triumphing in battle.
  • Exploration Mastery: Stealth, Perception, Athletics—skills for navigating dungeons, wilderness, and urban environments.
  • Social Influence: Persuasion, Insight, Intimidation—skills for navigating courts, taverns, and tense negotiations.
  • Arcane and Divine Knowledge: Arcana, Religion, Ritual—skills for understanding and wielding magic.
  • Wilderness Survival: Survival, Animal Handling—skills for thriving beyond civilization.
  • Technical Expertise: Medicine, Thievery—skills for healing wounds and bypassing obstacles.

Fantasy skills often interact with magic, monsters, and mythic stakes. A failed Stealth check might wake a dragon. A successful Persuasion check might avert a war. The world is larger than life, and the skills reflect that scope.

For proficiencies that enhance these skills, see Chapter 14 (Fantasy Proficiencies). For tags and conditions, see Chapter 18.

Combat Skills

Melee Combat — Combat

Description: Melee Combat is the art of close-quarters fighting with swords, axes, maces, and fists. A skilled combatant knows footwork, timing, and how to exploit openings.

Default Actions: - Strike Opponent: DC 14-16 — Attack an enemy in melee range. - Disarm or Trip: DC 16-18 — Attempt to disarm or knock an opponent prone. - Defend Ally: DC 16 — Intercept an attack meant for an ally. - Break Through Defenses: DC 18-20 — Overcome shields, armor, or defensive positions.

Synergies: Weapon Master proficiency, Elevated tag, Flanking tag.

Counters: Outnumbered tag, Restrained condition, Difficult Terrain tag.

GM Usage: Melee Combat drives the narrative forward in dangerous situations. Partials deal damage but suffer a counterattack or lose position. Failures miss or expose the attacker to harm. Use position (elevated, flanking) to add tactical depth.

Example: Kael charges the orc chieftain blocking the bridge. The GM calls for DC 16 (Strike Opponent). Kael rolls 18—his blade finds a gap in the chieftain’s armor, dealing a critical wound and forcing the orc to retreat.

Archery — Combat

Description: Archery is precision at range. An archer knows windage, elevation, and how to lead a moving target. Bows are quiet, deadly, and elegant.

Default Actions: - Shoot Target: DC 14-16 — Attack a target within range. - Aimed Shot: DC 18-20 — Target a specific weak point (eye, rope, mechanism). - Suppressing Fire: DC 16 — Pin down enemies, forcing them into cover. - Quick Draw: DC 14 — Draw and fire in one fluid motion.

Synergies: Archer proficiency, Elevated tag, Clear Sight tag.

Counters: Obscuring tag, Wind tag, Close Quarters tag.

GM Usage: Archery excels at distance and positioning. Partials hit but graze or consume extra ammunition. Failures miss or alert enemies. Reward players who use terrain (elevation, cover) tactically.

Example: Lyra perches on a tower and targets the goblin war horn blower. The GM calls for DC 18 (Aimed Shot). Lyra rolls 19—the arrow pierces the horn, silencing it and preventing reinforcements.

Tactics — Combat

Description: Tactics is the skill of reading a battlefield, coordinating allies, and exploiting enemy weaknesses. A tactician sees patterns in chaos.

Default Actions: - Read Battlefield: DC 14-16 — Identify key terrain, threats, or opportunities. - Coordinate Attack: DC 16-18 — Grant allies advantage through positioning or timing. - Exploit Weakness: DC 16 — Identify and target an enemy’s vulnerability. - Rally Allies: DC 16-18 — Remove fear or disorganization from allies.

Synergies: First Aid proficiency, Elevated tag, Teamwork tag.

Counters: Chaotic Melee tag, Obscuring tag, Divided Forces tag.

GM Usage: Tactics rewards strategic thinking. Partials grant limited advantages or require sacrifices. Failures misread the situation or expose allies. Use this skill to empower group play and reward planning.

Example: During a goblin ambush, Theron uses Tactics to read the battlefield (DC 16). He rolls 17—he identifies the goblin shaman directing the attack. The party focuses fire, eliminating the shaman and breaking the goblins’ morale.

Exploration Skills

Stealth — Exploration

Description: Stealth is the art of moving unseen and unheard. A skilled infiltrator knows how to exploit shadows, time patrols, and minimize noise.

Default Actions: - Sneak Past Guards: DC 14-18 — Move through an area without being detected. - Hide in Shadows: DC 14-16 — Conceal yourself in low light or cover. - Shadow Tail: DC 16-18 — Follow someone without being noticed. - Conceal Object: DC 12-14 — Hide an item on your person or in an environment.

Synergies: Cloaked condition, Dim tag, Crowded tag.

Counters: Alert tag, Tracking Dogs tag, Brightly Lit tag.

GM Usage: Stealth creates tension and enables infiltration. Partials succeed but trigger suspicion clocks or force risky positions. Failures alert enemies or create complications. Reward preparation (scouting, distractions).

Example: Mira infiltrates the castle during a festival. The Crowded tag grants Advantage, but the Alert Guards tag raises DC to 16. Mira rolls 17—she slips past the guards unnoticed and reaches the vault.

Perception — Exploration

Description: Perception is knowing where to look and what to listen for. A perceptive character catches ambushes, notices details, and finds hidden clues.

Default Actions: - Spot Ambush: DC 16-18 — Detect hidden threats before they strike. - Search Area: DC 14-18 — Find hidden doors, traps, or clues. - Track Movement: DC 14-16 — Follow tracks, blood trails, or disturbances. - Read Environment: DC 14 — Notice subtle changes or out-of-place details.

Synergies: Tracker proficiency, Elevated tag, Quiet Environment tag.

Counters: Obscuring tag, Dim tag, Chaotic tag.

GM Usage: Perception reveals information that changes choices. Partials find clues but miss context or take extra time. Failures overlook threats or clues. Use this skill to gate crucial information.

Example: Asha searches the abandoned library for the hidden codex. The GM calls for DC 16 (Search Area). Asha rolls 18—she notices a loose stone in the fireplace, revealing a secret compartment.

Athletics — Exploration/Combat

Description: Athletics is raw physical capability—climbing, jumping, swimming, grappling. It turns obstacles into opportunities and foes into cargo.

Default Actions: - Climb Wall or Cliff: DC 14-18 — Ascend vertical surfaces. - Leap Gap: DC 14-16 — Jump across chasms or rooftops. - Swim Against Current: DC 16-18 — Navigate rough water. - Grapple Opponent: Opposed Check — Restrain or pin an enemy.

Synergies: Climber proficiency, Rope tag, Teamwork tag.

Counters: Slick tag, Exhausted condition, Heavy Armor tag.

GM Usage: Athletics makes terrain tactical. Partials succeed but take time or risk position. Failures result in falls, failed jumps, or broken grips. Reward creativity (using ropes, teamwork).

Example: Kael climbs a crumbling tower to reach the griffon’s nest. The GM calls for DC 18 (Climb Wall). Kael rolls 16 (partial)—he reaches the nest but dislodges stones, alerting the griffon.

Social Skills

Persuasion — Social

Description: Persuasion is matching truth to motive. A persuasive character knows how to frame requests, appeal to values, and build rapport.

Default Actions: - Request Favor: DC 14-20 — Ask someone to help, share information, or make concessions. - Sway Crowd: DC 18-20 — Influence public opinion or mob behavior. - Negotiate Deal: DC 16-18 — Reach mutually beneficial agreements. - Inspire Allies: DC 14-16 — Motivate allies to take action or persevere.

Synergies: Diplomat proficiency, Reputation tag, Court Etiquette tag.

Counters: Hostile tag, By-the-Book tag, Distrustful condition.

GM Usage: Persuasion resolves social conflicts. Partials gain partial concessions or create new obligations. Failures entrench opposition or offend. Tie success to clear, achievable goals.

Example: Elara negotiates with the bandit leader to release hostages. The GM calls for DC 18 (Negotiate Deal). Elara rolls 19—the bandits agree to release the hostages in exchange for safe passage out of the valley.

Insight — Social

Description: Insight reads the silence between words. An insightful character catches lies, gauges moods, and perceives hidden motives.

Default Actions: - Read Motive: DC 14-18 — Discern someone’s true intentions or feelings. - Detect Lie: Opposed Check — Determine if someone is deceiving you. - Gauge Mood: DC 12-14 — Assess the emotional state of a person or group. - Spot Deception: DC 16-18 — Identify forged documents or disguises.

Synergies: Diplomat proficiency, Quiet Room tag, Familiar with Subject tag.

Counters: Deceptive tag, Masked Emotions tag, Chaotic Environment tag.

GM Usage: Insight reveals leverage and truth. Partials provide incomplete or ambiguous reads. Failures mislead or offend the target. Use this skill to expose hidden conflicts.

Example: Theron suspects the merchant is lying about the artifact’s origin. The GM calls for an opposed Insight check. Theron rolls 18; the merchant rolls 14. Theron catches the merchant’s nervous tell—the artifact is stolen.

Intimidation — Social

Description: Intimidation is the art of projecting threat. An intimidating character knows how to leverage fear, status, or consequences to compel action.

Default Actions: - Coerce Compliance: DC 14-18 — Force someone to cooperate through fear. - Break Morale: DC 16-18 — Cause enemies to flee or surrender. - Extract Information: DC 16-20 — Compel someone to reveal secrets. - Establish Dominance: DC 14-16 — Assert control over a situation or group.

Synergies: Reputation (Fearsome) tag, Armed tag, Elevated Position tag.

Counters: Defiant tag, Protected tag, Group Support tag.

GM Usage: Intimidation achieves compliance through fear. Partials gain cooperation but create resentment or future complications. Failures provoke violence or resistance. Balance short-term gains with long-term consequences.

Example: Kael confronts the cultist guarding the ritual chamber. The GM calls for DC 16 (Coerce Compliance). Kael rolls 18—the cultist drops his weapon and flees, shouting a warning to his comrades.

Arcane and Divine Skills

Arcana — Arcane

Description: Arcana is the study of magical principles, spell structures, and arcane phenomena. A scholar of the arcane can identify enchantments, dispel magic, and understand mystical forces.

Default Actions: - Identify Magic: DC 14-18 — Recognize spell effects, enchanted items, or magical creatures. - Dispel Effect: DC 16-20 — Unravel or suppress magical effects. - Recall Lore: DC 14-18 — Remember information about arcane history, entities, or phenomena. - Decipher Runes: DC 16-20 — Translate magical inscriptions or glyphs.

Synergies: Scribe proficiency, Library tag, Arcane Focus tag.

Counters: Obfuscation tag, Chaotic Magic tag, Forbidden Knowledge tag.

GM Usage: Arcana unlocks magical mysteries. Partials identify partial information or require additional research. Failures misidentify effects or trigger wards. Use this skill to gate magical solutions.

Example: Lyra examines the glowing runes on the doorway. The GM calls for DC 16 (Decipher Runes). Lyra rolls 17—the runes are a ward against undead. She disables the ward, allowing the party to enter.

Religion — Divine

Description: Religion is knowledge of deities, sacred texts, and divine rituals. A scholar of religion can recognize holy symbols, understand celestial hierarchies, and perform sacred rites.

Default Actions: - Recall Divine Lore: DC 14-18 — Remember information about gods, saints, or divine creatures. - Identify Sacred Site: DC 14-16 — Recognize temples, shrines, or consecrated ground. - Perform Rite: DC 16-18 — Conduct blessings, consecrations, or purifications. - Commune with Divine: DC 18-20 — Seek guidance or favor from a deity.

Synergies: Ritualist proficiency, Sacred Ground tag, Holy Symbol tag.

Counters: Desecrated tag, Warded Against Divine tag, Faithless condition.

GM Usage: Religion connects characters to divine forces. Partials receive incomplete guidance or require offerings. Failures offend divine powers or fail to activate sacred effects. Use this skill to provide divine intervention or moral stakes.

Example: Asha consecrates the defiled altar to banish the restless spirits. The GM calls for DC 18 (Perform Rite). Asha rolls 19—the altar glows with divine light, and the spirits find peace.

Ritual — Arcane/Divine

Description: Ritual is the performance of complex, time-intensive magical or divine ceremonies. Rituals require preparation, components, and precision.

Default Actions: - Perform Ritual: DC 16-22 — Execute a prepared ritual (divination, summoning, binding, etc.). - Improvise Ritual: DC 20-22 — Adapt or create a ritual on the fly. - Disrupt Ritual: DC 16-18 — Interrupt or sabotage an ongoing ritual. - Prepare Components: DC 14-16 — Gather and prepare materials for a ritual.

Synergies: Ritualist proficiency, Sacred Ground tag, Arcane Focus tag.

Counters: Desecrated tag, Interrupted tag, Incomplete Components tag.

GM Usage: Rituals are high-stakes, time-consuming actions. Partials succeed but create unintended consequences or require additional costs. Failures cause backlash or summon unintended entities. Use rituals for dramatic, narrative-shifting moments.

Example: Theron performs a divination ritual to locate the stolen crown. The GM calls for DC 18 (Perform Ritual). Theron rolls 16 (partial)—the vision is fragmentary, showing the crown in a dark forest but not the exact location.

Wilderness Skills

Survival — Wilderness

Description: Survival is the art of thriving beyond civilization. A survivalist knows how to find food, water, and shelter, and how to navigate treacherous terrain.

Default Actions: - Forage for Food: DC 12-16 — Find edible plants, berries, or game. - Track Creature: DC 14-18 — Follow tracks, signs, or disturbances. - Predict Weather: DC 14-16 — Anticipate storms, temperature shifts, or environmental hazards. - Build Shelter: DC 14-16 — Construct temporary shelter from natural materials.

Synergies: Huntsman proficiency, Forest tag, Seasonal Bounty tag.

Counters: Barren Land tag, Storm tag, Winter tag.

GM Usage: Survival sustains the party in the wilderness. Partials find resources but in limited quantities or with complications (poisonous plants nearby, shelter that leaks). Failures waste time or expose the party to hazards.

Example: The party is lost in the mountains during a blizzard. The GM calls for DC 18 (Build Shelter and Predict Weather). The survivalist rolls 17 (partial)—the shelter holds, but it is cramped and cold. The party suffers the Chilled condition until they reach warmth.

Animal Handling — Wilderness

Description: Animal Handling is the skill of communicating with and controlling animals. A handler knows how to calm, train, and command beasts.

Default Actions: - Calm Animal: DC 14-18 — Soothe a frightened or aggressive animal. - Command Mount: DC 14-18 — Direct a trained animal to perform tasks. - Train Animal: DC 16-20 (Downtime) — Teach an animal new tricks or behaviors. - Speak to Companion: DC 12-14 — Interpret the needs or warnings of a bonded animal.

Synergies: Beastmaster proficiency, Treats tag, Bonded Companion tag.

Counters: Frightened condition (on animal), Predators tag, Hostile Environment tag.

GM Usage: Animal Handling creates allies and solves problems. Partials calm animals temporarily or require extra time. Failures spook animals or provoke defensive behavior. Use this skill to turn beasts into assets.

Example: Kael encounters a wounded griffon blocking the mountain pass. The GM calls for DC 16 (Calm Animal). Kael rolls 18—the griffon allows Kael to approach and bandage its wing. The griffon becomes a temporary ally.

Technical Skills

Medicine — Technical

Description: Medicine is the art of preserving life. A healer knows anatomy, remedies, and how to stabilize the dying.

Default Actions: - Stabilize Dying Ally: DC 14 — Prevent an ally from dying. - Treat Poison or Disease: DC 16-18 — Identify and counteract toxins or illness. - Heal Wounds: DC 14-18 (Downtime) — Restore health over time with care and rest. - Perform Surgery: DC 18-20 — Remove arrows, set bones, or address internal injuries.

Synergies: First Aid proficiency, Healer’s Kit tag, Clean Environment tag.

Counters: Filth Fever tag, Battlefield Chaos tag, Insufficient Supplies tag.

GM Usage: Medicine saves lives and removes conditions. Partials stabilize but leave complications (Weakened condition, ongoing pain). Failures worsen conditions or consume resources. Use this skill to create tense, life-or-death moments.

Example: After the battle, Lyra treats Kael’s arrow wound. The GM calls for DC 16 (Treat Wounds). Lyra rolls 15 (partial)—the wound is cleaned and bandaged, but Kael suffers the Weakened condition until he rests.

Thievery — Technical

Description: Thievery is the art of bypassing locks, disabling traps, and liberating valuables. A thief respects craftsmanship enough to outwit it.

Default Actions: - Pick Lock: DC 14-20 — Open locks without keys. - Disable Trap: DC 16-22 — Safely disarm mechanical or magical traps. - Sleight of Hand: DC 14-18 — Steal items, plant objects, or perform misdirection. - Appraise Value: DC 12-16 — Estimate the worth of items or identify fakes.

Synergies: Fine Tools tag, Dim Light tag, Distracted Guards tag.

Counters: Complex Lock tag, Magical Ward tag, Alert tag.

GM Usage: Thievery opens paths and solves puzzles. Partials succeed but trigger alarms, take extra time, or break tools. Failures lock mechanisms, trigger traps, or alert guards. Reward preparation and creativity.

Example: Mira attempts to pick the lock on the vault door. The GM calls for DC 18 (Pick Lock). Mira rolls 17 (partial)—the lock opens, but her tools break. She cannot pick another lock until she finds replacements.

Worked Examples

Example 1: Infiltrating the Castle

Situation: The party needs to infiltrate the duke’s castle to recover stolen documents. Mira (Stealth expert) scouts ahead.

Action: The GM calls for Stealth (DC 16, Sneak Past Guards). The Crowded (festival) tag grants Advantage, but the Alert Guards tag raises the DC. Mira rolls 17 (success).

Outcome: Mira slips past the guards unnoticed and signals the party. They enter the castle without alerting the watch.

Example 2: Negotiating with Bandits

Situation: Elara tries to negotiate with bandits holding hostages. The bandits are desperate but not cruel.

Action: The GM calls for Persuasion (DC 18, Negotiate Deal). Elara offers safe passage in exchange for the hostages. She rolls 19 (success).

Outcome: The bandits agree. They release the hostages and retreat into the forest. Elara earns the Trusted Negotiator tag with the local villagers.

Example 3: Dispelling the Ward

Situation: The party encounters a warded door blocking access to the crypt. Lyra attempts to dispel the ward.

Action: The GM calls for Arcana (DC 18, Dispel Effect). Lyra rolls 16 (partial).

Outcome: The ward weakens but does not fully dissipate. The party can enter, but the ward triggers a minor alarm, starting a 6-segment clock: “Guards Arrive.”

Example 4: Tracking the Beast

Situation: The party tracks a wounded wyvern through the mountains. The tracker uses Survival.

Action: The GM calls for Survival (DC 16, Track Creature). The tracker rolls 18 (success).

Outcome: The tracker finds fresh blood and claw marks leading to a cave. The party prepares for the confrontation.

Using Fantasy Skills

Fantasy skills reward heroism, tactical thinking, and bold action. When using these skills:

  • Embrace High Stakes: Failed Stealth can wake dragons. Successful Persuasion can prevent wars. Let the stakes match the genre.
  • Reward Preparation: Players who scout, gather information, and plan should gain advantages.
  • Use Clocks for Long-Term Threats: Track enemy reinforcements, spreading plagues, or collapsing dungeons with clocks (see Chapter 05).
  • Layer Combat and Exploration: Let skills interact. Perception spots the ambush. Athletics reaches the high ground. Tactics coordinates the counterattack.

For proficiencies that enhance these skills, see Chapter 14 (Fantasy Proficiencies). For tags and conditions, see Chapter 18 (Tags and Conditions Glossary).

Chapter 09: Horror/Mystery Genre Skills

Horror and mystery games thrive on investigation, tension, and the slow unraveling of terrible truths. These skills turn clues into narratives, fear into survival, and the unknown into something you can name—even if naming it does not make it less dangerous. They are grounded in psychological depth, forensic detail, and the creeping realization that some doors should not have been opened.

This chapter provides ready-to-use skills for horror and mystery games—whether gothic horror, cosmic dread, noir detective stories, or occult investigations. Use these skills when your game features hidden truths, fragile sanity, and the price of knowledge.

Genre Overview

Horror and mystery skills emphasize:

  • Investigation: Research, Forensics, Deduction—skills for uncovering hidden truths and connecting evidence.
  • Psychological Resilience: Composure, Read Intent, Manipulation—skills for navigating fear, reading people, and maintaining control.
  • Occult Knowledge: Occult Lore, Ritual Knowledge—skills for understanding and confronting supernatural forces.
  • Survival Under Pressure: Urban Survival, Evasion, First Aid—skills for escaping danger and staying alive.
  • Social Interrogation: Interview, Deceive—skills for extracting information and constructing false identities.

Horror and mystery skills often carry psychological costs. Learning the truth might mean nightmares. Confronting the occult might mean trauma. Failed checks do not just delay progress—they erode sanity, trust, and safety.

For proficiencies that enhance these skills, see Chapter 15 (Horror/Mystery Proficiencies). For tags and conditions, see Chapter 18.

Investigation Skills

Research — Exploration

Description: Research is the art of finding answers in archives, databases, and forgotten texts. A skilled researcher knows how to navigate libraries, cross-reference sources, and separate fact from rumor.

Default Actions: - Search Archives: DC 14-18 — Find historical records, newspaper clippings, or obscure references. - Cross-Reference Clues: DC 16-18 — Connect disparate pieces of information into a coherent narrative. - Identify Source: DC 14-16 — Determine the origin or authenticity of a document or artifact. - Translate Obscure Text: DC 18-20 — Decipher old languages, codes, or cryptic notes.

Synergies: Archivist proficiency, Library tag, Quiet Environment tag.

Counters: Disorganized Archives tag, Restricted Access tag, Time Pressure.

GM Usage: Research reveals context and history. Partials provide incomplete information or lead to new questions. Failures waste time or uncover misleading sources. Use this skill to gate crucial backstory.

Example: Evelyn searches the university archives for records of the Blackwood family. The GM calls for DC 16 (Search Archives). Evelyn rolls 18—she finds letters mentioning a “ritual gone wrong” in 1887, pointing her toward the estate’s cellar.

Forensics — Technical

Description: Forensics is the science of reading crime scenes and physical evidence. Blood spatter, fingerprints, chemical residue—each tells a story if you know how to listen.

Default Actions: - Analyze Crime Scene: DC 16-18 — Determine cause of death, sequence of events, or evidence of struggle. - Identify Substance: DC 16-20 — Recognize poisons, drugs, or unusual chemicals. - Collect Evidence: DC 14-16 — Preserve and document physical evidence without contamination. - Reconstruct Timeline: DC 18-20 — Piece together the sequence of events from physical evidence.

Synergies: Forensic Kit tag, Laboratory tag, Methodical Approach tag.

Counters: Contaminated Scene tag, Time Pressure, Poor Lighting tag.

GM Usage: Forensics provides objective truths in a world of lies. Partials reveal partial information or require follow-up testing. Failures contaminate evidence or miss crucial details. Use this skill to anchor investigations in physical reality.

Example: Marcus examines the body found in the warehouse. The GM calls for DC 18 (Analyze Crime Scene). Marcus rolls 19—he determines the victim was poisoned hours before being moved, and finds traces of arsenic under the fingernails.

Deduction — Exploration

Description: Deduction is the skill of assembling clues into conclusions. A deductive mind sees patterns, eliminates impossibilities, and narrows possibilities to truth.

Default Actions: - Connect Clues: DC 16-18 — Synthesize disparate evidence into a coherent theory. - Eliminate Suspects: DC 14-16 — Rule out impossible scenarios or alibis. - Predict Behavior: DC 16-18 — Anticipate a suspect’s next move based on patterns. - Spot Inconsistencies: DC 14-18 — Identify contradictions in statements or evidence.

Synergies: Detective proficiency, Quiet Reflection tag, Complete Evidence tag.

Counters: Overwhelming Information tag, Red Herrings tag, Time Pressure.

GM Usage: Deduction turns clues into answers. Partials provide plausible but incomplete theories. Failures lead to false conclusions or dead ends. Use this skill to reward thorough investigation.

Example: After gathering evidence, Clara uses Deduction to identify the killer. The GM calls for DC 18 (Connect Clues). Clara rolls 19—she realizes the butler’s alibi contradicts the blood spatter pattern. The butler is the killer.

Psychological Skills

Composure — Psychological

Description: Composure is the skill of maintaining control when terror claws at your mind. It is steady breathing in the dark, rational thought in chaos, and the refusal to break.

Default Actions: - Resist Fear: DC 14-18 — Avoid panic when confronted with horror. - Suppress Trauma: DC 16-20 — Function despite psychological wounds or disturbing revelations. - Maintain Focus: DC 14-16 — Stay calm under pressure or during interrogation. - Rally Allies: DC 16-18 — Help others resist fear or despair.

Synergies: Calm Mind tag, Safe Space tag, Trusted Companion tag.

Counters: Frightened condition, Alone tag, Overwhelming Horror tag.

GM Usage: Composure determines whether characters break or endure. Partials resist fear but suffer lingering effects (Shaken condition, nightmares). Failures result in panic, freeze responses, or psychological conditions. Use this skill to create tense, emotional moments.

Example: The investigator opens the locked room and finds the ritual site. The GM calls for DC 16 (Resist Fear). The investigator rolls 14 (partial)—she does not flee, but gains the Shaken condition, suffering Disadvantage on social checks until she rests.

Read Intent — Social

Description: Read Intent is the skill of perceiving what others hide—fear, guilt, aggression, deception. It sees through masks and reads the body’s truth.

Default Actions: - Detect Lie: Opposed Check — Determine if someone is deceiving you. - Gauge Threat: DC 14-16 — Assess if someone is dangerous or unstable. - Read Emotion: DC 12-16 — Identify someone’s true emotional state. - Spot Tells: DC 16-18 — Recognize patterns of behavior that reveal intent.

Synergies: Psychiatrist proficiency, Quiet Room tag, Familiarity with Subject tag.

Counters: Masked Emotions tag, Chaotic Environment tag, Deceptive condition.

GM Usage: Read Intent exposes hidden truths and motives. Partials provide ambiguous or incomplete reads. Failures mislead or provoke the subject. Use this skill to create paranoia and doubt.

Example: The detective interviews the widow. The GM calls for an opposed Read Intent check. The detective rolls 17; the widow rolls 13. The detective notices the widow’s relief rather than grief—she wanted her husband dead.

Manipulation — Social

Description: Manipulation is the art of shaping perception and behavior. A manipulator knows how to exploit fears, desires, and biases to achieve their goals.

Default Actions: - Plant Suggestion: DC 16-18 — Subtly influence someone’s beliefs or actions. - Gaslight: DC 18-20 — Make someone doubt their own perceptions or memory. - Exploit Fear: DC 16-18 — Use fear to compel compliance or silence. - Build Dependence: DC 18-20 (Downtime) — Make someone emotionally reliant on you.

Synergies: Charismatic tag, Isolated Target tag, Trusted Position tag.

Counters: Strong-Willed tag, Support Network tag, Aware of Manipulation tag.

GM Usage: Manipulation achieves goals through psychological control. Partials succeed but create suspicion or resentment. Failures expose the manipulation or provoke backlash. Use this skill carefully—it can darken tone and erode trust.

Example: The cult leader uses Manipulation to convince a follower to sabotage the investigation. The GM calls for DC 18 (Plant Suggestion). The leader rolls 19—the follower believes the sabotage is their own idea and carries it out.

Occult Skills

Occult Lore — Arcane/Divine

Description: Occult Lore is knowledge of hidden things—forbidden rituals, ancient entities, and the laws that govern the unseen. This knowledge comes with a price.

Default Actions: - Identify Entity: DC 16-20 — Recognize supernatural creatures, spirits, or entities. - Recall Ritual: DC 16-20 — Remember details of occult practices or ceremonies. - Interpret Symbols: DC 14-18 — Decipher occult glyphs, sigils, or markings. - Ward Against Evil: DC 16-18 — Create protective charms or barriers.

Synergies: Occult Scholar proficiency, Library tag, Forbidden Texts tag.

Counters: Obfuscation tag, Chaotic Magic tag, Sanity Cost.

GM Usage: Occult Lore reveals dangerous truths. Partials provide incomplete information or trigger psychological costs (Obsessed condition, nightmares). Failures mislead or attract unwanted attention from entities. Use this skill to gate supernatural solutions and create existential dread.

Example: The investigator examines the summoning circle. The GM calls for DC 18 (Interpret Symbols). The investigator rolls 17 (partial)—she identifies the entity as a lesser demon but suffers the Obsessed condition, unable to stop thinking about the ritual.

Ritual Knowledge — Arcane/Divine

Description: Ritual Knowledge is the practical application of occult practices—performing rites, consecrations, and bindings. Rituals require preparation, components, and willpower.

Default Actions: - Perform Protective Rite: DC 16-18 — Ward a location or person against supernatural intrusion. - Banish Entity: DC 18-22 — Force a spirit or entity to leave the material plane. - Consecrate Ground: DC 16-18 — Sanctify a location to weaken supernatural threats. - Disrupt Ritual: DC 16-20 — Interrupt or sabotage an ongoing occult ceremony.

Synergies: Medium proficiency, Sacred Ground tag, Ritual Components tag.

Counters: Desecrated Ground tag, Interrupted tag, Sanity Cost.

GM Usage: Ritual Knowledge allows characters to confront the supernatural directly. Partials succeed but create complications (partial banishment, attracted entities). Failures cause backlash (psychological trauma, possessed conditions). Use this skill for climactic, high-stakes moments.

Example: The medium performs a banishment ritual to expel the ghost haunting the mansion. The GM calls for DC 20 (Banish Entity). The medium rolls 18 (partial)—the ghost is weakened and confined to the attic but not fully banished. A 4-segment clock starts: “Ghost Regains Strength.”

Survival Skills

Urban Survival — Exploration

Description: Urban Survival is the skill of navigating dangerous cities—finding shelter, avoiding threats, and securing resources when the streets turn hostile.

Default Actions: - Find Shelter: DC 14-16 — Locate safe places to hide or rest. - Scavenge Resources: DC 14-18 — Find food, water, or supplies in urban environments. - Navigate Safely: DC 16-18 — Move through dangerous areas without attracting attention. - Read Street Dynamics: DC 14-16 — Identify safe routes, gang territories, or police patrols.

Synergies: Streetwise proficiency, Crowded tag, Local Knowledge tag.

Counters: Lockdown tag, Hostile Territory tag, Winter tag.

GM Usage: Urban Survival sustains characters in hostile cities. Partials find limited resources or risky shelter. Failures attract danger or waste time. Use this skill to create tension in urban chases and investigations.

Example: After escaping the cultists, the investigator needs shelter. The GM calls for DC 16 (Find Shelter). The investigator rolls 15 (partial)—she finds an abandoned building but it is also being used by squatters who may betray her.

Evasion — Exploration

Description: Evasion is the art of escape—shaking pursuers, hiding in plain sight, and creating distance when violence is not an option.

Default Actions: - Lose Pursuer: Opposed Check — Escape someone following you. - Hide in Crowds: DC 14-16 — Blend into public spaces to avoid detection. - Create Misdirection: DC 16-18 — Leave false trails or confuse pursuers. - Emergency Exit: DC 16-18 — Find and use escape routes under pressure.

Synergies: Urban Survivalist proficiency, Crowded tag, Dim Light tag.

Counters: Tracking Dogs tag, Open Terrain tag, Exhausted condition.

GM Usage: Evasion creates chase scenes and narrow escapes. Partials create temporary distance or require sacrifices (dropped items, risky routes). Failures result in capture or injury. Use this skill to build tension and urgency.

Example: The detective is pursued by the killer through the subway. The GM calls for an opposed Evasion check. The detective rolls 18; the killer rolls 15. The detective loses the killer in the crowd and escapes.

First Aid — Technical

Description: First Aid is emergency medical care—stopping bleeding, treating shock, and stabilizing injuries until proper help arrives.

Default Actions: - Stabilize Injury: DC 14-16 — Stop bleeding or prevent shock. - Treat Wounds: DC 14-18 — Clean and bandage injuries to prevent infection. - Revive Unconscious: DC 16-18 — Bring someone back from unconsciousness. - Treat Poison or Toxin: DC 18-20 — Identify and counteract ingested substances.

Synergies: Field Medic proficiency, First Aid Kit tag, Clean Environment tag.

Counters: Chaotic Scene tag, Insufficient Supplies tag, Severe Injury tag.

GM Usage: First Aid keeps characters alive in dangerous situations. Partials stabilize but leave complications (Weakened condition, scarring). Failures worsen injuries or consume supplies. Use this skill to create life-or-death tension.

Example: After the car crash, the investigator treats her partner’s head wound. The GM calls for DC 16 (Stabilize Injury). The investigator rolls 15 (partial)—the bleeding stops, but the partner gains the Concussed condition and suffers Disadvantage on Perception checks.

Social Skills

Interview — Social

Description: Interview is the skill of extracting information through conversation—building rapport, asking the right questions, and reading between the lines.

Default Actions: - Build Rapport: DC 14-16 — Establish trust and openness with a subject. - Extract Information: DC 16-18 — Guide a subject toward revealing useful details. - Conduct Formal Interview: DC 16-20 — Question a suspect or witness systematically. - Detect Evasion: DC 16-18 — Notice when someone is avoiding questions or lying.

Synergies: Detective proficiency, Quiet Room tag, Recorded Session tag.

Counters: Hostile Subject tag, Lawyer Present tag, Time Pressure.

GM Usage: Interview reveals information and builds narratives. Partials provide partial truths or create new questions. Failures provoke silence or false information. Use this skill to pace investigations and create dramatic reveals.

Example: The detective interviews the janitor who found the body. The GM calls for DC 16 (Extract Information). The detective rolls 18—the janitor reveals he saw a woman in a red coat leaving the building shortly before the body was discovered.

Deceive — Social

Description: Deceive is the art of constructing false narratives and hiding truth. A skilled deceiver knows how to lie convincingly, create false identities, and manipulate perception.

Default Actions: - Tell Convincing Lie: Opposed Check — Deceive someone about facts, intent, or identity. - Create False Identity: DC 16-20 (Downtime) — Construct a believable cover story and documentation. - Misdirect Attention: DC 14-16 — Draw focus away from what you want hidden. - Maintain Cover: DC 16-18 — Sustain a false identity under scrutiny.

Synergies: Actor proficiency, Disguise tag, Chaotic Environment tag.

Counters: Familiar Face tag, Documented Records tag, Skeptical Observer tag.

GM Usage: Deceive enables infiltration and misdirection. Partials succeed but create suspicion or require follow-up lies. Failures expose the deception or provoke investigation. Use this skill to create tension and moral complexity.

Example: The investigator poses as a reporter to gain access to the crime scene. The GM calls for DC 16 (Maintain Cover). The investigator rolls 18—the police officer believes the cover story and grants access.

Worked Examples

Example 1: Investigating the Murder

Situation: The detective examines the study where the victim was found. Blood spatter, scattered papers, and a broken window suggest struggle.

Action: The GM calls for Forensics (DC 18, Analyze Crime Scene). The detective rolls 19 (success).

Outcome: The detective determines the victim was struck from behind, fought back, and tried to escape through the window. The blood trail leads outside—the killer chased the victim into the garden.

Example 2: Resisting Cosmic Horror

Situation: The investigator opens the vault and sees the altar to the Outer Dark—pulsing with wrongness, covered in alien glyphs.

Action: The GM calls for Composure (DC 18, Resist Fear). The investigator rolls 15 (partial).

Outcome: The investigator does not flee or faint, but gains the Shaken condition (Disadvantage on social checks) and suffers nightmares. The GM adds a 4-segment clock: “Sanity Erodes.”

Example 3: Banishing the Spirit

Situation: The medium performs a ritual to banish the vengeful ghost from the orphanage.

Action: The GM calls for Ritual Knowledge (DC 20, Banish Entity). The medium rolls 18 (partial).

Outcome: The ghost is weakened and confined to the basement but not fully banished. The GM starts a clock: “Ghost Regains Strength” (6 segments). The party must finish the ritual before the ghost breaks free.

Using Horror/Mystery Skills

Horror and mystery skills reward careful investigation, psychological resilience, and strategic thinking. When using these skills:

  • Layer Clues: Provide multiple clues through different skills—Research reveals history, Forensics reveals physical evidence, Deduction synthesizes both.
  • Use Psychological Costs: Failed Composure or Occult Lore checks can inflict conditions (Shaken, Obsessed, Traumatized). Make knowledge dangerous.
  • Pace Revelations: Use clocks to track investigation progress, pursuing threats, or eroding sanity.
  • Reward Preparation: Players who gather evidence, plan rituals, and secure resources should gain advantages.

For proficiencies that enhance these skills, see Chapter 15 (Horror/Mystery Proficiencies). For tags and conditions, see Chapter 18 (Tags and Conditions Glossary).

Chapter 10: Modern Genre Skills

Modern games focus on contemporary challenges—navigating bureaucracy, hacking networks, operating vehicles, negotiating deals, and surviving urban conflict. These skills turn technology, expertise, and social capital into tools for solving problems. They are grounded in real-world professions, tactical operations, and the complexities of modern life.

This chapter provides ready-to-use skills for modern and contemporary games—whether espionage thrillers, urban crime dramas, disaster response, or everyday professional challenges. Use these skills when your game features modern technology, urban environments, and realistic consequences.

Genre Overview

Modern skills emphasize:

  • Professional Expertise: Law, Medicine, Finance, Administration—skills for navigating institutional systems and specialized knowledge.
  • Technical Capability: Hacking, Engineering, Driving—skills for operating and manipulating modern technology.
  • Urban Navigation: Networking, Negotiate, Streetwise—skills for building connections and moving through social landscapes.
  • Tactical Operations: Firearms, Surveillance, Infiltration—skills for direct action and covert operations.

Modern skills often require specific tools, licenses, or access. A Hacking check might require a laptop and internet connection. A Medicine check might need medical supplies. Failed checks can trigger legal consequences, reputational damage, or systemic obstacles.

For proficiencies that enhance these skills, see Chapter 16 (Modern Proficiencies). For tags and conditions, see Chapter 18.

Professional Skills

Law — Professional

Description: Law is knowledge of legal systems, regulations, and procedures. A skilled legal practitioner knows how to navigate courts, draft contracts, and exploit loopholes.

Default Actions: - Legal Research: DC 14-18 — Find precedents, statutes, or case law. - Draft Contract: DC 16-18 — Create legally binding agreements. - Courtroom Argument: DC 16-20 — Present persuasive legal arguments. - Identify Violation: DC 14-16 — Recognize illegal activity or contractual breaches.

Synergies: Lawyer proficiency, Law Library tag, Case Files tag.

Counters: Corrupt System tag, Sealed Records tag, Time Pressure.

GM Usage: Law navigates legal systems and protects rights. Partials provide partial victories (reduced sentences, delayed proceedings). Failures result in lost cases or legal exposure. Use this skill to create institutional obstacles and victories.

Example: The lawyer defends a whistleblower in court. The GM calls for DC 18 (Courtroom Argument). The lawyer rolls 19—the jury acquits the whistleblower, and the corrupt corporation faces public scrutiny.

Medicine — Professional

Description: Medicine is the practice of diagnosing, treating, and preventing illness and injury. A skilled doctor knows anatomy, pharmacology, and emergency procedures.

Default Actions: - Diagnose Illness: DC 14-18 — Identify medical conditions from symptoms. - Treat Injury or Illness: DC 16-20 — Provide medical care to restore health. - Perform Surgery: DC 18-22 — Conduct complex medical procedures. - Prescribe Treatment: DC 14-16 — Recommend medications or therapies.

Synergies: Doctor proficiency, Medical Equipment tag, Hospital tag.

Counters: Insufficient Supplies tag, Critical Condition tag, Time Pressure.

GM Usage: Medicine saves lives and solves medical mysteries. Partials stabilize but leave complications (Weakened condition, side effects). Failures worsen conditions or consume resources. Use this skill for life-or-death scenarios and long-term care.

Example: The doctor treats a gunshot wound in a makeshift clinic. The GM calls for DC 18 (Treat Injury). The doctor rolls 17 (partial)—the patient stabilizes but gains the Weakened condition and requires hospital care within 24 hours.

Finance — Professional

Description: Finance is the skill of managing money, analyzing markets, and navigating economic systems. A financial expert knows how to trace funds, assess risk, and manipulate investments.

Default Actions: - Analyze Finances: DC 14-18 — Review accounts, budgets, or financial records. - Trace Funds: DC 16-20 — Follow money trails through transactions and accounts. - Secure Loan or Investment: DC 16-18 — Negotiate financial backing. - Spot Fraud: DC 16-20 — Identify embezzlement, money laundering, or financial crimes.

Synergies: Accountant proficiency, Financial Records tag, Software Access tag.

Counters: Encrypted Records tag, Offshore Accounts tag, Time Pressure.

GM Usage: Finance reveals economic power and corruption. Partials provide incomplete information or create exposure. Failures mislead or trigger investigations. Use this skill to uncover conspiracies and manipulate resources.

Example: The accountant traces illegal campaign donations. The GM calls for DC 18 (Trace Funds). The accountant rolls 19—she uncovers a shell company funneling money to the senator, providing evidence for prosecution.

Administration — Professional

Description: Administration is the skill of navigating bureaucracy, managing projects, and coordinating resources. An administrator knows how to file paperwork, expedite processes, and manipulate systems.

Default Actions: - Navigate Bureaucracy: DC 14-18 — Expedite permits, licenses, or approvals. - Organize Project: DC 16-18 — Coordinate teams, schedules, and resources. - Audit Records: DC 14-16 — Review documentation for errors or omissions. - Secure Access: DC 16-18 — Obtain clearances or authorizations.

Synergies: Administrator proficiency, Office Access tag, Proper Documentation tag.

Counters: Red Tape tag, Hostile Bureaucrat tag, Time Pressure.

GM Usage: Administration unlocks institutional resources and access. Partials succeed but require extra time or create obligations. Failures delay progress or trigger scrutiny. Use this skill to navigate realistic obstacles.

Example: The fixer needs building permits expedited for the safehouse. The GM calls for DC 16 (Navigate Bureaucracy). The fixer rolls 18—the permits are approved within 48 hours, no questions asked.

Technical Skills

Hacking — Technical

Description: Hacking is the art of bypassing digital security—breaching networks, spoofing credentials, and extracting data. A hacker knows systems, exploits, and how to cover their tracks.

Default Actions: - Breach Network: DC 16-20 — Gain unauthorized access to systems. - Extract Data: DC 16-18 — Download files or information without detection. - Spoof Credentials: DC 18-20 — Create false digital identities or clearances. - Cover Tracks: DC 16-20 — Erase evidence of intrusion.

Synergies: Network Admin proficiency, Laptop tag, Remote Access tag.

Counters: Firewall tag, Air-Gapped System tag, Active Monitoring tag.

GM Usage: Hacking unlocks digital secrets and access. Partials succeed but leave traces or trigger alerts. Failures lock systems, trigger alarms, or expose the hacker. Use this skill to create digital heists and investigations.

Example: The hacker breaches the corporation’s server to find evidence of fraud. The GM calls for DC 18 (Breach Network and Extract Data). The hacker rolls 19—she downloads encrypted files and exits without triggering alarms.

Engineering — Technical

Description: Engineering is the skill of designing, building, and repairing mechanical and electrical systems. An engineer knows physics, materials, and how to solve structural problems.

Default Actions: - Repair System: DC 14-18 — Fix damaged machinery or electronics. - Design Solution: DC 16-20 — Create or modify equipment for specific needs. - Analyze Structure: DC 14-18 — Assess stability, weaknesses, or failure points. - Improvise Fix: DC 16-20 — Jury-rig temporary solutions under pressure.

Synergies: Mechanic proficiency, Workshop tag, Quality Tools tag.

Counters: Damaged Tools tag, Complex System tag, Time Pressure.

GM Usage: Engineering solves technical problems and creates opportunities. Partials succeed but require extra time or create fragile solutions. Failures worsen damage or create hazards. Use this skill for problem-solving and improvisation.

Example: The engineer repairs the elevator in a burning building to evacuate survivors. The GM calls for DC 18 (Repair System under pressure). The engineer rolls 17 (partial)—the elevator works but only for one trip before failing.

Driving — Exploration/Combat

Description: Driving is the skill of operating vehicles under pressure—pursuits, evasive maneuvers, and precision control. A skilled driver knows when to accelerate, brake, and turn.

Default Actions: - Pursuit: Opposed Check — Chase or evade another vehicle. - Evasive Maneuvers: DC 16-18 — Avoid obstacles or attacks while driving. - Precision Driving: DC 16-20 — Navigate tight spaces or difficult terrain. - Ram or Block: DC 16-18 — Use the vehicle as a weapon or barrier.

Synergies: Driver proficiency, Performance Vehicle tag, Clear Road tag.

Counters: Traffic Jam tag, Damaged Vehicle tag, Poor Weather tag.

GM Usage: Driving creates dynamic chase scenes and escapes. Partials succeed but damage the vehicle or lose distance. Failures crash, stall, or lose control. Use this skill for high-stakes action sequences.

Example: The agent pursues the assassin through city streets. The GM calls for an opposed Driving check. The agent rolls 18; the assassin rolls 15. The agent closes the distance and forces the assassin’s car into a dead-end alley.

Social Skills

Networking — Social

Description: Networking is the art of building and leveraging professional relationships. A networker knows who to call, what favors are owed, and how to make connections.

Default Actions: - Find Contact: DC 14-18 — Locate someone with specific expertise or access. - Call in Favor: DC 16-18 — Request help from a professional connection. - Build Relationship: DC 14-16 (Downtime) — Establish new professional ties. - Secure Introduction: DC 16-18 — Gain access to influential people or groups.

Synergies: PR Specialist proficiency, Professional Event tag, Reputation tag.

Counters: Burned Bridges tag, Isolated Industry tag, Time Pressure.

GM Usage: Networking unlocks resources and information. Partials provide limited help or create obligations. Failures burn connections or reveal vulnerabilities. Use this skill to navigate professional and social landscapes.

Example: The journalist needs a source inside the police department. The GM calls for DC 16 (Find Contact). The journalist rolls 18—she calls a former colleague now working as a detective who agrees to share information off the record.

Negotiate — Social

Description: Negotiate is the skill of reaching agreements through persuasion, compromise, and strategic concessions. A negotiator knows when to push, when to yield, and when to walk away.

Default Actions: - Broker Deal: DC 16-18 — Reach mutually beneficial agreements. - De-escalate Conflict: DC 16-20 — Calm tense situations before they turn violent. - Secure Better Terms: DC 18-20 — Improve contract conditions or agreements. - Hostage Negotiation: DC 18-22 — Convince someone to release captives peacefully.

Synergies: Negotiator proficiency, Calm Environment tag, Leverage tag.

Counters: Hostile Parties tag, Time Pressure, Ultimatum tag.

GM Usage: Negotiate resolves conflicts and secures resources. Partials achieve partial concessions or create new obligations. Failures entrench positions or escalate tensions. Use this skill for high-stakes social encounters.

Example: The negotiator tries to convince the bank robber to surrender. The GM calls for DC 20 (Hostage Negotiation). The negotiator rolls 21—the robber releases the hostages and surrenders peacefully.

Streetwise — Exploration/Social

Description: Streetwise is the skill of navigating urban underworlds—knowing who runs what, where to find contraband, and how to avoid trouble.

Default Actions: - Find Black Market: DC 14-18 — Locate illegal goods or services. - Gather Rumors: DC 14-16 — Learn street-level information or gossip. - Avoid Trouble: DC 16-18 — Navigate gang territories or dangerous areas safely. - Secure Safehouse: DC 16-18 — Find temporary, untraceable shelter.

Synergies: Streetwise proficiency, Urban Environment tag, Local Knowledge tag.

Counters: Crackdown tag, Outsider tag, Hostile Territory tag.

GM Usage: Streetwise unlocks urban resources and information. Partials provide limited access or create debts. Failures attract danger or expose the character. Use this skill for urban investigations and survival.

Example: The fixer needs illegal weapons for the operation. The GM calls for DC 16 (Find Black Market). The fixer rolls 18—she locates a dealer willing to sell untraceable firearms for the right price.

Tactical Skills

Firearms — Combat

Description: Firearms is the skill of operating pistols, rifles, and shotguns effectively. A trained shooter knows marksmanship, weapon handling, and tactical use of cover.

Default Actions: - Controlled Fire: DC 14-16 — Engage targets accurately. - Suppressing Fire: DC 16-18 — Pin enemies behind cover. - Precision Shot: DC 18-20 — Target specific weak points (lock, tire, weapon). - Quick Draw: DC 14-16 — Draw and fire in one motion.

Synergies: Firearms Expert proficiency, Cover tag, Clear Sight tag.

Counters: Obscuring tag, Crowded Environment tag, Malfunctioning Weapon tag.

GM Usage: Firearms resolves combat quickly and lethally. Partials hit but graze or consume ammunition. Failures miss or create collateral damage. Use this skill for realistic, dangerous confrontations.

Example: The agent engages armed mercenaries in a warehouse. The GM calls for DC 16 (Controlled Fire from cover). The agent rolls 18—she drops two mercenaries with precise shots, forcing the others to retreat.

Surveillance — Exploration/Technical

Description: Surveillance is the art of watching without being seen—setting up cameras, tailing suspects, and gathering intelligence.

Default Actions: - Set Up Watch: DC 14-18 — Install cameras or monitoring equipment. - Tail Target: DC 16-18 — Follow someone without detection. - Monitor Communications: DC 16-20 — Intercept calls, emails, or messages. - Analyze Footage: DC 14-16 — Review recordings for useful information.

Synergies: Surveillance Tech proficiency, Drone tag, Remote Access tag.

Counters: Counter-Surveillance tag, Crowded Environment tag, Encrypted Communications tag.

GM Usage: Surveillance gathers intelligence and tracks threats. Partials provide incomplete information or risk detection. Failures expose the surveillance or waste resources. Use this skill for investigations and preparation.

Example: The detective sets up surveillance on the suspect’s apartment. The GM calls for DC 16 (Set Up Watch). The detective rolls 18—cameras and audio are installed undetected, providing 24/7 monitoring.

Infiltration — Exploration

Description: Infiltration is the skill of gaining unauthorized access to restricted areas—bypassing security, social engineering, and blending in.

Default Actions: - Bypass Security: DC 16-20 — Defeat locks, alarms, or access controls. - Social Engineering: DC 16-18 — Talk your way past guards or receptionists. - Blend In: DC 14-18 — Pose as authorized personnel. - Exfiltrate: DC 16-18 — Exit a restricted area without detection.

Synergies: Lockpicking proficiency, Disguise tag, Crowded Event tag.

Counters: Biometric Security tag, Active Patrols tag, Alert Status tag.

GM Usage: Infiltration enables covert operations and espionage. Partials succeed but trigger suspicion or leave traces. Failures trigger alarms or expose the infiltrator. Use this skill for heist and espionage scenarios.

Example: The spy infiltrates the embassy during a diplomatic reception. The GM calls for DC 18 (Blend In and Bypass Security). The spy rolls 19—she gains access to the secure wing undetected and retrieves the documents.

Worked Examples

Example 1: Hacking the Server

Situation: The hacker needs to breach the corporation’s server to find evidence of fraud.

Action: The GM calls for Hacking (DC 18, Breach Network and Extract Data). The hacker rolls 19 (success).

Outcome: The hacker downloads encrypted files containing evidence of illegal offshore accounts. She exits without triggering alarms and begins decrypting the files.

Example 2: Car Chase Through the City

Situation: The agent pursues the assassin through downtown traffic.

Action: The GM calls for an opposed Driving check. The agent rolls 18; the assassin rolls 15.

Outcome: The agent closes the gap and forces the assassin’s car into a dead-end alley. The assassin abandons the vehicle and flees on foot, triggering a foot chase (Evasion or Athletics).

Example 3: Negotiating the Hostage Release

Situation: The crisis negotiator attempts to convince the bank robber to release hostages.

Action: The GM calls for Negotiate (DC 20, Hostage Negotiation). The negotiator rolls 21 (success).

Outcome: The robber agrees to release the hostages in exchange for safe passage to a vehicle. The police honor the agreement, and the hostages are freed unharmed.

Using Modern Skills

Modern skills reward expertise, preparation, and strategic thinking. When using these skills:

  • Require Tools and Resources: Hacking needs a laptop. Medicine needs supplies. Firearms need ammunition. Make logistics matter.
  • Create Realistic Consequences: Failed Firearms checks can cause collateral damage. Failed Hacking can trigger investigations. Failed Negotiation can escalate to violence.
  • Use Clocks for Long-Term Operations: Track investigations, surveillance operations, or corporate takeovers with clocks (see Chapter 05).
  • Layer Professional and Tactical Skills: Combine Law with Networking to build a legal case. Combine Surveillance with Infiltration to plan a heist.

For proficiencies that enhance these skills, see Chapter 16 (Modern Proficiencies). For tags and conditions, see Chapter 18 (Tags and Conditions Glossary).

Chapter 11: Sci-Fi Genre Skills

Sci-fi games explore futures shaped by technology, alien civilizations, and the mysteries of space. These skills turn starships into homes, quantum physics into solutions, and first contact into diplomacy. They are grounded in advanced technology, xenoscience, and the unique challenges of operating beyond planetary boundaries.

This chapter provides ready-to-use skills for sci-fi games—whether space opera, hard science fiction, cyberpunk futures, or post-human settings. Use these skills when your game features faster-than-light travel, alien encounters, cybernetics, or advanced technology.

Genre Overview

Sci-fi skills emphasize:

  • Pilot and Navigation: Pilot Spacecraft, Navigate Hyperspace—skills for operating and navigating starships.
  • Technical Mastery: System Engineering, Cybernetics, Xenotech—skills for maintaining and manipulating advanced technology.
  • Scientific Expertise: Xenobiology, Physics, Chemistry—skills for understanding and exploiting scientific principles.
  • Combat Adaptation: Zero-G Combat, Energy Weapons—skills for fighting in space and with futuristic weapons.
  • Xenosocial Skills: Diplomacy (Aliens), Negotiate—skills for interacting with non-human species and cultures.

Sci-fi skills often depend on technology level and equipment. A Pilot Spacecraft check requires a functioning ship. A Cybernetics check requires tools and parts. Failed checks can result in cascading system failures, alien misunderstandings, or catastrophic breaches.

For proficiencies that enhance these skills, see Chapter 17 (Sci-Fi Proficiencies). For tags and conditions, see Chapter 18.

Pilot and Navigation Skills

Pilot Spacecraft — Exploration/Combat

Description: Pilot Spacecraft is the art of maneuvering ships through space—docking, evasive burns, combat maneuvers, and navigating debris fields. A skilled pilot knows thrust vectors, orbital mechanics, and how to coax speed from limited fuel.

Default Actions: - Dock with Station: DC 14-18 — Execute precision docking maneuvers. - Evasive Maneuvers: DC 16-18 — Avoid weapons fire or obstacles. - Combat Burn: DC 16-20 — Engage enemy ships or break pursuit. - Navigate Debris Field: DC 18-20 — Pilot through asteroid belts or wreckage.

Synergies: Starship Pilot proficiency, Clear Space tag, Responsive Ship tag.

Counters: Debris Field tag, Damaged Thrusters tag, Gravity Well tag.

GM Usage: Piloting creates dynamic space sequences. Partials succeed but damage the ship or consume extra fuel. Failures result in collisions, missed docks, or enemy hits. Use this skill for chases, combat, and tense navigation.

Example: The pilot navigates through an asteroid field to evade pirate ships. The GM calls for DC 18 (Navigate Debris Field). The pilot rolls 19—the ship weaves through the asteroids unscathed, losing the pursuers.

Navigate Hyperspace — Technical

Description: Navigate Hyperspace is the skill of plotting faster-than-light jumps—calculating safe routes, avoiding gravity wells, and accounting for stellar phenomena. A navigator knows charts, astrophysics, and how to read the void.

Default Actions: - Plot Jump: DC 16-20 — Calculate safe hyperspace routes. - Emergency Jump: DC 20-22 — Plot a jump under pressure without full calculations. - Identify Safe Exit: DC 16-18 — Find exit points that avoid hazards. - Adjust Mid-Jump: DC 18-22 — Recalculate route during faster-than-light travel.

Synergies: Astrogator proficiency, Star Charts tag, Calibrated Nav Computer tag.

Counters: Uncharted Space tag, Interference tag, Damaged Nav Systems tag.

GM Usage: Navigation gates interstellar travel. Partials succeed but require longer routes or emerge near hazards. Failures result in misjumps, emergence in dangerous zones, or system damage. Use this skill to create exploration and danger.

Example: The navigator plots an emergency jump to escape a fleet engagement. The GM calls for DC 22 (Emergency Jump). The navigator rolls 20 (partial)—the ship jumps but emerges near a stellar flare, suffering minor radiation damage.

Technical Skills

System Engineering — Technical

Description: System Engineering is the skill of maintaining, repairing, and optimizing starship systems—life support, power cores, shields, and propulsion. An engineer knows how to reroute power, patch leaks, and jury-rig failing systems.

Default Actions: - Repair System: DC 16-20 — Fix damaged ship systems under pressure. - Reroute Power: DC 16-18 — Shift power between systems for tactical advantage. - Bypass Lock or Safety: DC 16-20 — Override automated controls or security. - Stabilize Core: DC 18-22 — Prevent reactor meltdown or catastrophic failure.

Synergies: Systems Tech proficiency, Engineering Bay tag, Quality Parts tag.

Counters: Damaged Tools tag, Cascading Failures tag, Vacuum tag.

GM Usage: Engineering keeps ships operational. Partials succeed but create temporary fixes or require power sacrifices. Failures worsen damage or create new hazards. Use this skill for desperate repairs and tactical decisions.

Example: During combat, the engineer reroutes power from life support to shields. The GM calls for DC 16 (Reroute Power). The engineer rolls 18—shields strengthen, but the crew has 20 minutes of oxygen before life support must be restored.

Cybernetics — Technical

Description: Cybernetics is the art of integrating, maintaining, and upgrading biological-mechanical interfaces—implants, prosthetics, and neural enhancements. A cyberneticist knows wetware, biocompatibility, and how to prevent rejection.

Default Actions: - Install Implant: DC 16-20 (Downtime) — Surgically integrate cybernetic components. - Repair Augmentation: DC 16-18 — Fix damaged cybernetics or implants. - Upgrade System: DC 18-20 — Enhance existing implants or prosthetics. - Diagnose Rejection: DC 14-18 — Identify and treat cybernetic incompatibility.

Synergies: Cybernetics Tech proficiency, Medical Bay tag, Quality Implants tag.

Counters: Incompatible Biology tag, Insufficient Sterility tag, Damaged Implant tag.

GM Usage: Cybernetics enables transhumanism and augmentation. Partials succeed but create side effects (pain, instability, limited function). Failures cause rejection, infection, or malfunction. Use this skill for character customization and medical drama.

Example: The cyberneticist installs a neural interface in the hacker’s skull. The GM calls for DC 18 (Install Implant). The cyberneticist rolls 17 (partial)—the implant works but causes periodic headaches (Distracted condition during use).

Xenotech — Technical

Description: Xenotech is the study and application of alien technology—reverse-engineering devices, operating unfamiliar systems, and adapting alien tools to human use. A xenotech specialist knows pattern recognition, experimental methodology, and when not to press the glowing button.

Default Actions: - Identify Function: DC 16-20 — Determine what an alien device does. - Operate Device: DC 16-20 — Use alien technology safely. - Reverse Engineer: DC 20-22 (Downtime) — Understand and replicate alien tech. - Disable Safely: DC 18-20 — Deactivate alien systems without triggering defenses.

Synergies: Xenotech Specialist proficiency, Lab Equipment tag, Alien Schematics tag.

Counters: Unknown Principles tag, Incompatible Power tag, Defensive Systems tag.

GM Usage: Xenotech unlocks alien capabilities and mysteries. Partials provide partial understanding or trigger minor malfunctions. Failures activate defenses, damage the device, or cause unpredictable effects. Use this skill for exploration and discovery.

Example: The xenotech specialist examines a derelict alien ship’s control panel. The GM calls for DC 18 (Identify Function). The specialist rolls 19—she identifies the power routing controls and activates emergency lighting.

Scientific Skills

Xenobiology — Technical

Description: Xenobiology is the study of alien life—anatomy, behavior, ecology, and biochemistry. A xenobiologist knows how to analyze unknown organisms, predict behavior, and handle dangerous lifeforms safely.

Default Actions: - Analyze Organism: DC 16-20 — Study alien biology to understand capabilities or weaknesses. - Identify Threat Level: DC 14-18 — Assess if a lifeform is dangerous. - Treat Alien Injury: DC 18-20 — Provide medical care to non-human species. - Sample Safely: DC 16-18 — Collect biological samples without contamination or harm.

Synergies: Xenobiology Kit tag, Lab Facilities tag, Protective Gear tag.

Counters: Unknown Biology tag, Hostile Organism tag, Contaminated Environment tag.

GM Usage: Xenobiology enables understanding and interaction with alien life. Partials provide incomplete data or risk exposure. Failures result in incorrect conclusions, contamination, or provoked hostility. Use this skill for first contact and survival.

Example: The xenobiologist analyzes the creature attacking the colony. The GM calls for DC 18 (Analyze Organism). The xenobiologist rolls 19—she identifies a weak spot in the creature’s exoskeleton, granting the team Advantage on combat rolls.

Physics — Technical

Description: Physics is the understanding of fundamental forces—gravity, electromagnetism, radiation, and quantum mechanics. A physicist knows how to exploit physical laws, predict phenomena, and solve problems with math.

Default Actions: - Calculate Trajectory: DC 14-18 — Predict projectile paths, orbital mechanics, or collisions. - Identify Phenomenon: DC 16-20 — Recognize anomalies, radiation sources, or exotic physics. - Design Experiment: DC 18-20 — Create tests to explore unknown physics. - Exploit Physics: DC 18-22 — Use physical principles to solve problems (slingshot maneuvers, electromagnetic shielding).

Synergies: Quantum Physicist proficiency, Lab Equipment tag, Computational Models tag.

Counters: Unknown Variables tag, Limited Data tag, Time Pressure.

GM Usage: Physics provides scientific solutions and understanding. Partials succeed but require assumptions or simplified models. Failures miscalculate or create new problems. Use this skill for exploration and problem-solving.

Example: The physicist calculates a slingshot maneuver around a black hole to escape pursuit. The GM calls for DC 20 (Calculate Trajectory and Exploit Physics). The physicist rolls 21—the ship uses the black hole’s gravity to accelerate beyond the pursuers’ maximum speed.

Chemistry — Technical

Description: Chemistry is the study of matter, reactions, and compounds. A chemist knows how to synthesize substances, analyze compositions, and neutralize toxins.

Default Actions: - Analyze Substance: DC 14-18 — Identify chemical composition or properties. - Synthesize Compound: DC 16-20 — Create medicines, explosives, or materials. - Neutralize Toxin: DC 18-20 — Counteract poisons or corrosive substances. - Identify Hazard: DC 14-16 — Recognize dangerous chemicals or reactions.

Synergies: Lab Equipment tag, Chemical Database tag, Protective Gear tag.

Counters: Incomplete Samples tag, Unstable Compounds tag, Insufficient Materials tag.

GM Usage: Chemistry enables creation and analysis. Partials succeed but with impurities or limited quantities. Failures create hazards (explosions, toxic fumes) or waste materials. Use this skill for crafting and problem-solving.

Example: The chemist synthesizes a universal antidote for an alien toxin. The GM calls for DC 20 (Synthesize Compound). The chemist rolls 18 (partial)—the antidote works but only has enough for one dose.

Combat Skills

Zero-G Combat — Combat

Description: Zero-G Combat is the art of fighting in microgravity—controlling momentum, using handholds, and adapting tactics to three-dimensional space. A skilled zero-g combatant knows how to anchor, maneuver, and strike without spinning out of control.

Default Actions: - Melee Attack: DC 16-18 — Strike opponents while controlling momentum. - Grapple in Zero-G: Opposed Check — Restrain or position opponents. - Use Environment: DC 14-16 — Push off walls, use handholds, or leverage debris. - Ranged Combat: DC 16-20 — Compensate for recoil and lack of gravity.

Synergies: Zero-G Specialist proficiency, Handholds tag, Magnetic Boots tag.

Counters: Spin tag, Open Space tag, Disoriented condition.

GM Usage: Zero-G combat creates unique tactical challenges. Partials succeed but lose position or momentum. Failures spin out of control or miss entirely. Use this skill for space station battles and boarding actions.

Example: The marine grapples a pirate on the derelict station. The GM calls for an opposed Zero-G Combat check. The marine rolls 18; the pirate rolls 14. The marine pins the pirate against a bulkhead and disarms him.

Energy Weapons — Combat

Description: Energy Weapons is the skill of operating beam rifles, plasma pistols, and particle cannons—weapons that use focused energy instead of projectiles. An energy weapons specialist knows heat management, charge timing, and how to avoid overloads.

Default Actions: - Controlled Burst: DC 14-16 — Engage targets with precision fire. - Overcharge Shot: DC 18-20 — Fire high-damage shots at the risk of overheating. - Suppress Enemy: DC 16-18 — Pin enemies behind cover with sustained fire. - Disable Equipment: DC 18-20 — Target specific systems (locks, power conduits, weapons).

Synergies: Energy Weapons proficiency, Clear Sight tag, Charged Weapon tag.

Counters: Reflective Armor tag, Overheated Weapon tag, Energy Shield tag.

GM Usage: Energy weapons provide futuristic firepower. Partials hit but overheat or drain power. Failures miss, overheat dangerously, or splash collateral damage. Use this skill for sci-fi combat.

Example: The soldier targets the alien’s energy shield generator. The GM calls for DC 20 (Disable Equipment). The soldier rolls 21—the generator explodes, dropping the alien’s shields and exposing it to fire.

Social Skills

Diplomacy (Aliens) — Social

Description: Diplomacy (Aliens) is the skill of navigating cultural differences, non-human psychology, and xenosocial norms. A xenodiplomat knows how to avoid offense, build trust, and find common ground across species.

Default Actions: - First Contact Protocol: DC 16-20 — Establish peaceful communication with new species. - Negotiate Treaty: DC 18-22 — Reach agreements between human and alien factions. - Navigate Customs: DC 14-18 — Avoid cultural missteps or taboos. - Build Rapport: DC 16-18 — Establish trust and understanding with alien individuals.

Synergies: Diplomat proficiency, Translator Device tag, Cultural Database tag.

Counters: Hostile Species tag, Cultural Misunderstanding tag, Xenophobia tag.

GM Usage: Diplomacy enables peaceful coexistence and understanding. Partials succeed but create minor misunderstandings or require concessions. Failures offend, escalate tensions, or provoke hostility. Use this skill for first contact and interspecies relations.

Example: The diplomat negotiates mining rights with the insectoid hive. The GM calls for DC 18 (Negotiate Treaty). The diplomat rolls 19—the hive agrees to shared access in exchange for human medical technology.

Negotiate — Social

Description: Negotiate is the skill of reaching agreements across cultures, factions, and species—balancing interests, making concessions, and finding mutual benefit.

Default Actions: - Broker Deal: DC 16-18 — Reach commercial or political agreements. - Secure Resources: DC 16-20 — Obtain supplies, ships, or support through negotiation. - De-escalate Standoff: DC 18-20 — Prevent conflicts from turning violent. - Trade Information: DC 14-18 — Exchange intelligence or secrets fairly.

Synergies: Negotiator proficiency, Neutral Ground tag, Leverage tag.

Counters: Hostile Parties tag, Communication Barriers tag, Ultimatum tag.

GM Usage: Negotiation resolves conflicts and secures resources. Partials achieve partial concessions or create new obligations. Failures entrench positions or escalate tensions. Use this skill for diplomacy and trade.

Example: The trader negotiates for fuel and repairs at a neutral station. The GM calls for DC 16 (Broker Deal). The trader rolls 18—the station master agrees to provide supplies at a fair rate in exchange for navigation data on a nearby nebula.

Worked Examples

Example 1: Emergency Hyperspace Jump

Situation: The ship is under attack by a fleet. The navigator must plot an emergency jump without time for full calculations.

Action: The GM calls for Navigate Hyperspace (DC 22, Emergency Jump). The navigator rolls 20 (partial).

Outcome: The ship jumps successfully but emerges near a stellar flare. The GM starts a 4-segment clock: “Radiation Damage Accumulates.” The engineer must repair shielding before critical failure.

Example 2: Repairing the Reactor

Situation: The ship’s reactor is overloading after a hit. The engineer must stabilize it before it explodes.

Action: The GM calls for System Engineering (DC 20, Stabilize Core). The engineer rolls 18 (partial).

Outcome: The reactor stabilizes but power output is reduced to 60%. The ship can sustain life support and minimal thrust but cannot jump or use weapons until full repairs are made (Downtime).

Example 3: First Contact with Crystalline Species

Situation: The crew encounters a crystalline species communicating through light pulses. The diplomat must establish peaceful contact.

Action: The GM calls for Diplomacy (Aliens) (DC 18, First Contact Protocol). The diplomat rolls 19 (success).

Outcome: The diplomat successfully interprets the light pulses and establishes basic communication. The crystalline beings share coordinates to a safe anchorage and offer trade.

Using Sci-Fi Skills

Sci-fi skills reward technical expertise, adaptability, and bold exploration. When using these skills:

  • Require Technology and Equipment: Piloting requires a ship. Cybernetics requires tools. Physics requires computational models. Make technology integral.
  • Create Cascading Failures: Failed System Engineering can trigger reactor meltdowns. Failed Navigation can strand the crew. Let failures escalate tension.
  • Use Clocks for Long-Term Operations: Track ship repairs, hyperspace journeys, alien diplomacy, or reactor stability with clocks (see Chapter 05).
  • Layer Scientific and Tactical Skills: Combine Xenobiology with Combat to exploit weaknesses. Combine Physics with Piloting for advanced maneuvers.

For proficiencies that enhance these skills, see Chapter 17 (Sci-Fi Proficiencies). For tags and conditions, see Chapter 18 (Tags and Conditions Glossary).

Chapter 12: Proficiencies Introduction

Proficiencies represent the specialized training and mastery that separates someone who dabbles from someone who dedicates. Where skills define broad capabilities, proficiencies sharpen specific techniques into reliable advantages. They transform uncertain attempts into confident actions, reducing DCs, granting advantage, and unlocking possibilities that would otherwise be closed.

What Proficiencies Represent

Proficiencies are the product of deliberate practice. They reflect drills, repetitions, apprenticeships, and hard-won insights. A character with the Baker proficiency does not merely know how to mix ingredients—they understand temperature curves, rising times, and how to coax flavor from simple flour. A character with the Forensics proficiency does not just examine crime scenes—they preserve chain of custody, recognize trace evidence patterns, and extract information others would overlook.
