Modifier Quick Reference

Fast lookup for all modifiers, bonuses, and penalties.

Core Modifier Types

Skill Bonuses

From training and experience: - +0: Untrained - +1: Basic training - +2: Competent - +3: Skilled - +4: Expert - +5: Master

Apply to: Relevant skill checks

Situational Modifiers

From circumstances: - -4: Severe hindrance - -2: Moderate hindrance - +0: Standard conditions - +2: Moderate help - +4: Significant help

Apply to: Specific checks based on situation

Proficiency Bonuses

From specialized training: - +1 or +2: When using relevant proficiency - Advantage: When proficiency particularly applicable

Apply to: Checks involving proficiency

When To Apply Modifiers

Stack Everything Relevant

Typical check might include: - Skill bonus (+2) - Proficiency bonus (+1) - Situational modifier (+2) - Advantage (roll 2d6, take higher)

Example: Lockpicking with tools - Base roll: 2d6 - Thievery skill: +2 - Lockpicking proficiency: +1 - Quality tools: +2 - Total: 2d6 +5

Don’t Stack Same Type

Only one of each type applies: - One skill bonus (highest if multiple apply) - One proficiency bonus (if multiple, player chooses) - Situational modifiers stack unless same source

Advantage and Disadvantage

Advantage

Roll 2d6, take higher

Grant when: - Favorable position or preparation - Ally provides meaningful help - Opponent at disadvantage - Clever use of environment - Relevant proficiency applies exceptionally well

Examples: - High ground in combat - Assisted by ally - Perfect tools for job - Target is distracted - Extensive preparation

Disadvantage

Roll 2d6, take lower

Impose when: - Unfavorable position - Improvising or unprepared - Injured or impaired - Hostile environment - Active opposition

Examples: - Fighting while prone - Working in darkness - Exhausted or wounded - Rushed or time pressure - Terrible tools

Advantage/Disadvantage Interaction

Multiple sources of same: Doesn’t stack, still just one Advantage + Disadvantage: Cancel out, straight roll Can’t have both: If any of each, they cancel

Condition Modifiers

Physical Conditions

Wounded: - Disadvantage on physical actions (Athletics, Combat, etc.)

Exhausted: - Disadvantage on all actions

Stunned: - Lose next action

Prone: - Disadvantage on attacks - Enemies have advantage (melee) or disadvantage (ranged) against you

Restrained: - Cannot move - Disadvantage on attacks - Attackers have advantage

Blinded: - Disadvantage on attacks - Enemies have advantage against you

Mental/Social Conditions

Shaken: - Disadvantage on mental and social actions

Frightened: - Disadvantage on all actions while source visible - Cannot move closer to source

Confused: - Actions may be random or GM-directed

Beneficial Conditions

Empowered: - Advantage on relevant actions

Inspired: - Advantage on next check OR +2 bonus

Hidden: - Advantage on attacks from hiding - Enemies can’t directly target you

Defended: - +2 to defense OR attackers have disadvantage

Combat Modifiers

Positioning

High Ground: - +2 to attack OR advantage

Cover (Light): - +2 to defense OR attackers disadvantage

Cover (Heavy): - +4 to defense OR attackers major disadvantage

Flanking (if used): - +2 to attack OR advantage

Prone: - -2 to attack OR disadvantage

Range

Close (melee or adjacent): - No modifier

Medium Range: - No modifier for ranged - Disadvantage for thrown

Long Range: - -2 to attack OR disadvantage

Extreme Range: - Major disadvantage or auto-miss

Tactical

Surprised: - Lose first action - Enemies advantage first round

Outnumbered: - GM may grant advantage to multiple attackers

Charging: - +2 to attack but may expose you

Aiming (ranged): - Spend action to aim: +2 or advantage next attack

Environmental Modifiers

Lighting

Bright: - No modifier

Dim: - -2 to Perception - Disadvantage on precise tasks

Darkness: - -4 to Perception - Major disadvantage on most actions - Advantage for stealth

Weather

Clear: - No modifier

Rain/Wind: - -2 to ranged attacks - -2 to Perception

Heavy Storm: - Disadvantage on ranged attacks - Disadvantage on Perception - Movement hindered

Extreme (blizzard, hurricane): - Major disadvantage on most actions - Possible damage or forced movement

Terrain

Open Ground: - No modifier

Difficult Terrain: - Movement costs double - -2 to Athletics or disadvantage

Hazardous Terrain: - Risk of damage - Checks to move safely - Major disadvantage on complex actions

Gear and Equipment

Tools and Equipment

Improvised/Poor Tools: - -2 or disadvantage

Standard Tools: - No modifier (or enables attempt)

Quality Tools: - +2 or advantage

Master-crafted Tools: - +4 or major advantage

Weapons and Armor

Weapon Quality: - Improvised: -2 - Standard: +0 - Fine: +1 - Masterwork: +2

Armor Quality: - None: +0 defense - Light: +1 defense - Medium: +2 defense - Heavy: +3 defense but mobility penalty

Time Pressure

Ample Time: - +2 or advantage - Can retry failed checks - Auto-success on easy tasks

Standard Time: - No modifier

Rushed: - -2 or disadvantage - Risk of mistakes

Immediate/Panic: - Major disadvantage - Possible auto-failure on complex tasks

Assistance and Teamwork

Direct Assistance

One ally helps: - Advantage on check OR +2

Multiple helpers: - Still just advantage (doesn’t stack)

Expert helper: - Advantage plus maybe +1

Group Checks

Everyone rolls: - Success if majority succeed - OR each faces consequence individually

Combined Effort

Multiple PCs working together: - One PC leads, rolls with advantage - Others provide bonuses: +1 each (max +3)

Proficiency Examples

Common Proficiencies

  • Specific weapon: +1 with that weapon
  • Specific tool: +1 with that tool
  • Specific knowledge: +1 or advantage on related lore
  • Specific language: Enables communication

Stacking Examples

Example 1: Climbing

Base: 2d6 Athletics: +2 Climbing gear: +1 (proficiency) Roped by ally: +2 (situational) Total: 2d6 +5

Example 2: Persuasion

Base: 2d6 Persuasion: +3 Noble background: +1 (proficiency) Target is friendly: Advantage Total: 2d6 +4 with advantage

Example 3: Combat

Base: 2d6 Melee Combat: +2 Sword proficiency: +1 High ground: Advantage Total: 2d6 +3 with advantage

Quick Modifier Decision Tree

Step 1: What skill applies? - Add skill bonus

Step 2: Do any proficiencies apply? - Add +1 or +2 from best proficiency

Step 3: What are the conditions? - Good: +2 or advantage - Bad: -2 or disadvantage - Neutral: no change

Step 4: Calculate total - Roll 2d6 + all bonuses - Apply advantage/disadvantage - Compare to DC

Maximum Modifiers

Practical Limits

Skill bonuses: Usually +0 to +5 Proficiency bonuses: Usually +1 to +2 Situational modifiers: Usually -4 to +4 Total typical maximum: Around +10

Anything above +10 total is exceptional

Common Mistakes

Don’t

  • Stack advantage (only one applies)
  • Stack proficiencies (pick best one)
  • Apply skill bonus twice
  • Forget situational modifiers

Do

  • Add all different types of bonuses
  • Apply advantage separately
  • Consider conditions
  • Use common sense

Genre-Specific Modifiers

Cozy

  • Smaller modifiers overall (-2 to +2 typical)
  • Emphasis on advantage/disadvantage
  • Community help provides bonuses

Fantasy

  • Standard modifier system
  • Magic provides variety of bonuses
  • Legendary items give significant bonuses

Horror/Mystery

  • Emphasis on penalties and disadvantage
  • Few bonuses available
  • Conditions impactful

Modern

  • Technology provides bonuses
  • Situational modifiers important
  • Professional gear matters

Sci-Fi

  • Advanced tech provides major bonuses
  • Ship systems stack differently
  • AI assistance common

Quick Reference Summary

Typical Check:

2d6
+ Skill bonus (0 to +5)
+ Proficiency bonus (+1 or +2 if applicable)
+ Situational modifier (-4 to +4)
with Advantage or Disadvantage (if applicable)
vs DC (6 to 18)

Result: - 10+: Success - 7-9: Success with cost - 6-: Failure but story continues

Proficiency Catalog (All Genres)

Comprehensive list of proficiencies across all genres.

How Proficiencies Work

Proficiency = Specialized training or expertise

Mechanical Effect: - +1 or +2 bonus to relevant checks - OR advantage on checks - OR enables attempt at specialized task

When to Apply: - Task specifically matches proficiency - Player declares use - Makes fictional sense

Universal Proficiencies

Combat Proficiencies

Weapon Types: - Swords/Blades (+1) - Axes/Heavy weapons (+1) - Bows/Ranged (+1) - Thrown weapons (+1) - Polearms (+1) - Unarmed/Brawling (+1) - Improvised weapons (+1)

Combat Styles: - Dueling (+1 one-on-one) - Two-weapon fighting (+1) - Shield use (+1 defense) - Mounted combat (+1) - Formation fighting (+1 with allies)

Tactical: - Command (+1 leading troops) - Defensive tactics (+1 protection) - Ambush (+1 surprise attacks) - Retreat/Withdrawal (+1 escaping)

Social Proficiencies

Languages: - Each language is a proficiency - Enables communication - May grant +1 to social checks with speakers

Cultural Knowledge: - Specific culture (+1 or advantage) - Nobility/Royalty (+1 court) - Criminal underworld (+1 streetwise) - Military protocol (+1) - Religious traditions (+1)

Performance: - Specific instrument (+1) - Singing/Voice (+1) - Acting/Theater (+1) - Storytelling (+1) - Dance (+1) - Public speaking (+1)

Interpersonal: - Reading people (+1 Insight) - Negotiation (+1 Persuasion) - Intimidation tactics (+1) - Seduction/Charm (+1) - Diplomacy (+1)

Knowledge Proficiencies

Academic: - History (specific region/period) (+1) - Philosophy (+1) - Literature (+1) - Mathematics (+1) - Astronomy (+1) - Geography (+1)

Natural Sciences: - Biology/Anatomy (+1) - Botany/Herbalism (+1) - Zoology (+1) - Geology (+1) - Weather prediction (+1)

Practical Knowledge: - Appraisal/Valuation (+1) - Navigation (+1) - Cartography (+1) - First aid (+1) - Survival (terrain type) (+1) - Tracking (+1)

Technical Proficiencies

Crafting: - Smithing (+1) - Carpentry (+1) - Leatherworking (+1) - Tailoring/Sewing (+1) - Pottery/Ceramics (+1) - Glassblowing (+1) - Jewelry making (+1) - Cooking/Baking (+1) - Brewing/Distilling (+1)

Tools: - Lockpicks (+1) - Thieves’ tools (+1) - Disguise kit (+1) - Forgery kit (+1) - Poisoner’s kit (+1) - Herbalism kit (+1) - Musical instrument (specific) (+1)

Vehicles: - Riding (horses) (+1) - Driving (carts/wagons) (+1) - Sailing (+1) - Piloting (ships) (+1)

Cozy Proficiencies

Community and Social

Hospitality: - Innkeeping (+1) - Event planning (+1) - Hosting guests (+1) - Table service (+1)

Creating Custom Proficiencies

Guidelines

Good Proficiency: - Specific enough to be meaningful - Broad enough to use regularly - Enables cool character moments - Fits character concept

Too Broad: - “Combat” (use skills instead) - “Magic” (too general) - “Technology” (what aspect?)

Too Narrow: - “Opening red doors” - “Fighting only goblins” - “Tuesday negotiations”

Just Right: - “Lockpicking” - “Dragon lore” - “Starship piloting” - “Forensic analysis”

Proficiency Bonus Values

+1 Bonus

Standard proficiency: - Represents training - Applies regularly - Most common

+2 Bonus

Master proficiency: - Represents expertise - Requires special investment - Rare, requires GM approval

Advantage

Alternative to bonus: - When proficiency exceptionally relevant - One-time boost - At GM discretion

Enables Attempt

Some proficiencies required: - Can’t pick locks without proficiency - Can’t pilot starship without training - Can’t perform surgery untrained

Proficiency Selection

At Character Creation

Typical number: 2-4 proficiencies - Based on background - Reflects training and life experience - Should support character concept

Gaining New Proficiencies

During play: - Downtime training - Milestone advancement - Story-driven acquisition - Finding teachers/mentors

Using Proficiencies in Play

When Player Declares

PC: “I want to pick the lock using my lockpicking proficiency” GM: “Great, roll Thievery +2 for the proficiency”

When GM Suggests

GM: “You need to navigate through the storm. Anyone have sailing proficiency?” PC: “I do! Does that help?” GM: “Yes, advantage on the check”

When Enables Attempt

PC: “I want to hack the computer” GM: “Do you have hacking proficiency?” PC: “No” GM: “Then you can try but it’s disadvantage/higher DC”
